Both of them needed letters of introduction for passport applications to work abroad. It was decided to send letters to the British Consulate and the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau for assistance in issuing passports. (3) Fellow townsman Zhu Huajin came to the association, stating that his relative, Shan Jipin, was falsely accused of kidnapping by his wife, Wu, and was detained in court. He requested relief and assistance. Based on this, the legal counsel, lawyer Yu Hualong, was entrusted to defend him, and the court ruled him not guilty. (4) Fellow townsman Sun Yongnian came to the association, stating that his father, Sun Jingyu, who served as an ordnance officer in the 6th Regiment of the Fujian Provincial Security Team, was killed by mutinous soldiers of the 1st Company while returning to his post. Yongnian should fulfill his filial duty by going to Fujian to bring his father's coffin back to their hometown and requested a letter to local police officers for protection. It was decided to send a letter to the Fujian Provincial Police Bureau to instruct the police to provide protection. (5) Member Chen Caifu came to the association, stating that he carelessly caused a fire on the overhanging building at the entrance of Hongmao Lane on South Railway Station Road, which spread to the coal baskets placed under the building by members. Unexpectedly, the residents of the overhanging building falsely accused the member's partner, Ye Weishui, of endangering public safety and detained him for transfer to the court, requesting assistance and relief. It was decided to entrust legal counsel Yu Hualong to prepare a defense and send a letter to the Shanghai Jiangsu Local Court, requesting a fair trial to avoid injustice. (6) The association compiled the fifth edition of the member directory, which was printed by the Nanyang Printing Company. The company was scheduled to complete the printing and deliver it to the association this week. The proposal was to decide how to distribute the directory to the members. It was decided that those living far away would receive it by mail, while those living nearby would have it delivered by the teahouse. The meeting discussed over sixty cases of relief, mediation, and assistance, too many to detail. After the discussions, the meeting adjourned.

Deaf and Mute Old Woman Killed Crossing Tracks

In Qingning Temple, Pudong, at 5 PM on the 6th of this month, Qin Shen, a 52-year-old woman who was deaf and mute, was shopping at Wan Shun Sauce Garden. At that time, a Shangchuan bus was coming from the south, sounding its horn frequently. The woman did not hear it due to her deafness and crossed the tracks. The driver immediately braked, but it was too late, and she was hit, resulting in her death at the scene. The company reported the incident to the 9th Precinct of the 3rd District of the Public Security Bureau and notified the local bailiff to report to the Shanghai Local Court for inspection.

Letter

To the Editor: I am writing on behalf of my client, Chen Xiaobao, who stated that he read in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on the 30th of last month an article about Shen Ahong being arrested, which mentioned multiple accomplices, including Chen Xiaobao, etc., which was very shocking. Upon investigation, it is found that there are countless people in our country with the same surname and given name, which does not need to be debated. Moreover, Xiaobao travels to Shanghai to do business and also holds a position in a shipping company. He has never participated in any political party activities, nor has he taken any transgressive actions. The person referred to in the article is likely someone else, or it is a misunderstanding of hearsay. However, fearing that distant rumors will be misinterpreted, causing misunderstandings, and because the article involves suspicion of being reactionary, which is of great importance, he has to declare and defend himself. For this reason, he has entrusted your lawyer to write to various newspapers to declare the above. My client, Chen Xiaobao, is from eastern Zhejiang and has been employed in a commercial shipping company for several years. He has always been law-abiding and does not participate in political party activities. I hereby write to you on his behalf to declare the above. This is addressed to the Shanghai Newspaper. Lawyer Yang Shaozhi, June 7th.

Dear Editor: I have just read in your newspaper a news item about the Xixin'an Temple in Nanshi being harassed by itinerant monks, which does not quite correspond to the facts. This temple is a private temple of Shouleng and Shoushen, mainly for quiet meditation and chanting Buddha, and has no contact with the outside world. After Shoushen passed away, Shouleng presided over it for more than thirty years. The so-called Jianci nun is only staying temporarily in the temple, not the abbess. When the itinerant monks first came to harass the temple, in order to maintain the temple rules, Jianci was immediately ordered to leave the temple and was taken away by her original introducer, the Li family. Everything is unrelated to this temple. Your newspaper's report is inaccurate and concerns the reputation of this temple. I dare to write this letter without hesitation to declare and hope that it will be published in your newspaper's letter column for correction. Thank you very much. Xixin'an Temple Abbot Shouleng respectfully.

Dear Editor: The news about "The Rent Increase Wave in Penglai Market" published in your newspaper on the 4th of this month is completely inconsistent with the facts. The houses in this market were originally priced at 30 yuan per room when they were completed in March 1920. At that time, Shen Hengzhuang, Shanghai Shoe Room, Penglai Coffee Shop, and Wuzhou Pharmacy, etc., all agreed to rent them. Later, in May, when national product manufacturers joined, Chen Maiyun of Sanyou Industrial Society, Fang Jiange of China Enamel Factory, Li Xinpu of Family Industrial Society, and Pan Dechun of Renchangyong Material Factory, etc., negotiated with us, saying that they were all here to promote national products and reduce prices, and persuaded us to also reduce the house rental prices. Therefore, it was agreed that the rent for the 1920 year would be reduced to 10 yuan per room, and then increase by 5 yuan per room each year, with the expectation of making up the original 30 yuan in five years. This is an agreement reached between the landlord who extraordinarily reduced the price of the house in advance to accommodate the tenants, and the tenants who confirmed that they would gradually make up the original rent, and a contract and lease were signed, clearly stating that it is completely different from the ordinary rent increase situation. For this reason, most of the shops in this market who understand the truth still pay the rent monthly as agreed, without interruption. In the current situation, it seems like a rent increase, but based on the agreement, it cannot be said to be a rent increase in general. I especially ask you to correct this to clarify the facts and correct the hearing. I am deeply grateful. This is addressed to the editor of the Shanghai Newspaper, Penglai Market Preparatory Office, June 7, 1934.

Gratitude. I thank the Ministry of Railways for the gift of "Catalog of Books in the Library of the Ministry of Railways" and the Commercial Press for the gift of the 11th issue of the 32nd volume of Children's World and the 40th volume of Children's Pictorial. I write this to express my gratitude.

Reading Q&A

On the Contradictions of Life丨丨Answering Questions from Li Qing, He Guofen, and Luo Guangtao 1. The Question's Origin

This question was first raised by Mr. Li, and later letters were received from Mr. He and Mr. Luo, all seriously requesting a scientific understanding of this question. Mr. He said: "Although this is a very ordinary question, it is a question that all young people want to understand, because the life of modern Chinese youth is too contradictory. Confucianists are distressed and confused in contradiction, and the brave either hold their heads high and move forward regardless of everything for their goals, or, on the contrary, commit suicide happily." Indeed, this is a serious question that has been forgotten and needs to be scientifically addressed. Now, the questions raised by Mr. Li and others are revealed below:

1. Is the contradiction of life a kind of morbidity, a deviation from the norm of life?

2. How to explain the contradiction between a person's thoughts and actions, the contradiction between thoughts and thoughts, and the contradiction between actions and actions? 3. How to overcome contradictions in behavior?

3. The phenomenon of contradictions in life is determined by the contradictions in the life process itself.

Mr. Luo deeply blames himself for the contradictions in his life, highly praises, and envies a life without contradictions. He hopes that his life can be like a pool of autumn water, completely eliminating contradictions. Needless to say, he denies that a reasonable life would have contradictions. Mr. Luo cited many ancient sages and wise men to prove that the lives of great personalities are completely without contradictions? A life with contradictions is only the life of ordinary people. Are these words completely correct? Of course, they are not correct. Because Mr. Luo sees life as too simple and abstract. He ignores that the life process itself is a process of contradiction and struggle. Life is nothing more than the continuation of contradictions, and the contradictory phenomena manifested in behavior only illustrate the contradiction and struggle of life itself. This has nothing to do with the inferiority or superiority of people, and there is no mystery involved.

However, where does the root of this mistake of Mr. Luo lie? This is undoubtedly due to the following reasons. Because society despises the contradictory phenomena in a person's life, and uses contradictions as a tool to weigh or attack people. Therefore, only those who are straightforward like Mr. Li, Mr. He, and Mr. Luo are willing to confess the contradictions in their own lives, and others are unwilling to easily admit it. Some people have to wait until their contradictions are noticed by others before they blush, half-swallowingly, and reluctantly admit it in shyness. Some people pretend to be "solemn and inviolable," claiming that they have no contradictions in their lives. In fact, this is all social hypocrisy. Since the life process is a process of contradiction and struggle, not having contradictions means not having a life. Ordinary people always tend to imagine that a great person is different from ordinary people in everything, which is completely a misunderstanding. He ignores that since he is a person, he must have the commonality of human beings, and at the same time, he also has his uniqueness. There is an old saying in China that "heroes are often ordinary people," which reveals the truth. Because heroes are originally people, although they have extraordinary aspects, they should also have the general qualities of ordinary people. Otherwise, they will all turn into supermen. If we break this concept, whether the contradictions in our lives are on the surface of behavior or "internal," we don't need to keep them secret, nor do we need to think it is a shameful thing. It is not a morbidity of life, nor is it out of the norm of life. It is just a very ordinary phenomenon in the life process. (To be continued)

Special Article: A Refutation of Foreign Misinterpretations of the Pilotage Treaty (6): Declaration of the Preparatory Committee of the China Pilotage Association

Furthermore, what we want these journalists to understand clearly is that the 1868 regulations, in any case, were regulations that China willingly and voluntarily established. They were a form of China's internal affairs. We have endured this burden for sixty-six years. Even without the January 28th Incident, we were already determined that we could no longer tolerate it. Therefore, today, our government's clear order to reclaim pilotage rights and abolish the Tongzhi 7th Year Regulations is not only a wise internal policy that the government should implement, but it also truly represents the genuine public opinion of all of China. Therefore, no matter what kind of sophistry or curses these journalists engage in, since we cannot find any basis in the treaties, we can only regard the speakers as hypocritical, deceptive, and simply cursing.

We still have something to say to these journalists: what we know is that national rights are above all else, and nothing else can be compared to them, let alone foreign shipping companies. Speaking of the tonnage of ships entering and leaving Shanghai, fortunately, China still has six million tons; otherwise, according to the journalists' intention, wouldn't even the Huangpu River have to be ceded to foreigners? The journalists of this publication also threaten that if China reclaims pilotage rights in the future, foreign ships will dock at Wusong. This shows the journalists' lack of common sense. Generally speaking, progress is normal, while going backward is abnormal. The Shanghai docks have already been developed to such an extent. Perhaps only the journalists of this publication have this kind of insight to advise them to abandon this and choose that.

Furthermore, regarding this publication's slander of Chinese pilots, the publication repeatedly asserts that Chinese pilots do not possess even the minimum level of foreign pilot trainees. We initially do not know on what basis they say this. Furthermore, their discussions of piloting skills, etc., are superficial and can only be used to deceive laymen. Therefore, what we want to announce to all countries and sectors is that, standing in the position of pilots, we are very willing to accept this publication's criticism of "local knowledge and the method of pointing." This is because we believe that what the job of a pilot requires is precisely familiarity with all local conditions (such as water depth, currents, wind direction effects, etc.), supplemented by considerable ship-handling experience, which is sufficient. Anything else is just deceptive talk. Because after the ship enters the port, even the simplest bearing in ordinary navigation is unnecessary. The only piloting method is the method of pointing, that is, where the bow points and where the stern points, which is already sufficient. For example, when entering the Wusongkou, the bow must face the Wusong Lighthouse and be aligned with the light beacon in front of the tower to ensure a minimum water depth of thirty feet. Also, for example, when entering the port near Chenjiazhui at night, when approaching the light beacon opposite Chenjiazhui, one must wait until the light on the north side of Donggou is fully exposed before changing the needle to steer towards the center of the channel to obtain the deepest draft. There are countless other similar examples, and it is unnecessary to list them all. Such a method is the method of pointing. We have not been in contact with foreign pilots and do not know how much better they are than us. If the journalists of this publication would not hesitate to teach us, we would be very welcome.

Finally, we have heard a rumor that last year, a certain port in China held a pilot examination, and a Chinese person took the exam and achieved excellent results. Thereupon, a certain foreign examiner raised an objection and strongly demanded that this person be re-examined. At that time, the chairman said, "Why didn't you ask during the exam and insist on asking after the exam? This is unfair and unacceptable." Thereupon, the foreigner raised the difficulty that the Chinese person did not have the ability to pilot and navigate. Unexpectedly, this angered the manager of the pilot association, who said to the foreigner, "A pilot only needs to have all the local knowledge and ship-handling skills, and the rest is just talk. Even if our great ability to pilot and navigate is very good, we still break ships and sink ships. I think your countrymen are the same. Take away their piloting and navigation skills." If this rumor is reliable, then the journalists of this publication can rest easy. Perhaps the minds of sailors are simple, and in an unfair situation, they will speak out with justice and truth, unlike those hypocritical gentlemen who hold the Bible in their left hand and the butcher knife in their right, wanting to kill people and pretending to act on behalf of heaven.

Finally, we still have to say something incessantly, that is, there are several important ports in the United Kingdom, such as Liverpool, where the number of ships entering and leaving and the congestion of waterways in the port are even greater than in Shanghai Port. However, the qualifications of their pilots do not necessarily require them to have been captains. This is a fact. The journalist is British. How can he not know about his own country's affairs? Why doesn't he mention it in his article? Isn't he trying to deceive the audience with alarming words to sell his cunning? We also know that once this kind of fact is revealed, it will become dull and tasteless. However, because of the relationship that blood is thicker than water, we have to express our sincere feelings to the journalists of this publication, and these are just straightforward words. (The End)

Chunqiu

Records of the Lingering Fragrance of the Imperial Incense

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

The name of the nine-tone gong (九音鑼) comes from the distinct tones produced by its nine small copper gongs. My particular admiration for it stems from the sweetness and remarkable charm of its sound. It's played by gently striking the gongs with a thin wooden stick, which has a hard wooden ball, about the size of an abacus bead, attached to its end. This hard wood creates an especially clear and resonant tone.

The nine distinct sounds of the nine-tone gong correspond to the nine musical notes actually used in ancient Chinese musical notation, much like the 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, and 7 used today. These are represented by the characters 工, 四, 上, 尺, 五, 一, 六, 萬, and 合. How these nine characters came to be selected for musical notation and what meanings they hold are questions I cannot answer. Beyond myself, perhaps most people couldn't answer them either. This is because the origins are long past, and everyone just learns the old tunes without bothering to delve into the underlying reasons.

Next is the sheng (笙). Among Chinese musical instruments, the sheng is considered one of the oldest and most unique. Its shape resembles a Buddha's hand. It has twenty-four slender bamboo pipes, each of a different length, with small holes along their sides. The player blows into a car-handle-like base while simultaneously pressing and releasing these small holes with their fingers. Like the nine-tone gong, this produces various distinct sounds corresponding to the nine musical notes mentioned earlier. However, due to the slenderness of the bamboo pipes, the sound can't be very high, and playing it is very tiring for the player. (52)

Old Man Wang the Eighth

— Yu Wen

Before the January 28th Incident, Old Man Wang the Eighth would come to my place every two or three days to have his clothes washed. After the Shanghai battle, I moved, and I haven't seen the old man since.

Speaking of this Old Man Wang the Eighth, there's something admirable about him. In his younger days, he was a sailor on an ocean liner, had been to various European and American countries, and could speak fluent English. He was very amiable and diligent. Although he was old, he didn't act like it. Even when people called him "Old Wang Ba" (Old Turtle), he didn't argue with them. Although he had been abroad and could speak foreign languages, he didn't show off in front of others. If he saw foreign police officers bullying people for no reason, or drunken foreign sailors hitting people at will, he would step forward to interfere and reason with them. He didn't wear Western suits, didn't speak foreign languages, didn't like Western ways, and didn't like to use foreign goods. He wore homespun clothes and used Chinese goods.

Although Old Man Wang was a good person, his two sons were unfilial. They both sold Japanese goods! Perhaps it was because they were of mixed race? It turns out that Old Man Wang's wife was a foreign woman he brought back from England years ago.

The day before yesterday, I ran into Old Man Wang on the street, whom I hadn't seen for a long time. After we parted, I learned that his "foreign goods" wife had died. After the January 28th Incident, his two "mixed-race" sons continued their Japanese goods business. Old Man Wang repeatedly tried to persuade them not to, but they wouldn't listen, and now he has separated from them.

Later, I thought that Old Man Wang was really admirable. The modern men and women who love to use foreign goods are not as good as him! But when I thought of Old Man Wang's sons still working as traitors, I couldn't help but curse twice, "Dog bastards!"

Visiting the Horse

— Friend of Bo Le (A mythical horse connoisseur)

In the "Brief Biographies of People" column on the 18th of last month, there was an article by Xun Ziju, "A Record of a Talent," which was about a student who had studied at Tokyo Imperial University. Fearing that no one would consult him after returning to China, he did not want to return to the country and only wanted to live his life in Japan as an "old student" (a simplified name for old overseas students). He studied chemistry, pharmacology, and biology. He could make his own cosmetics to help with his living expenses.

In the article, the author attributed this deformed situation to the country and society, believing that it was "a feeling of a fine horse not meeting Bo Le!" In fact, there are many Bo Les in society who are looking for fine horses!

Now, a famous figure in the domestic goods industry, after seeing this article, felt endless sympathy for this fine horse who was not meeting his opportunity. He intends to seek out this fine horse so that he can develop his talent for a thousand miles.

However, because Xun Ziju did not write down his friend's name and address, this Mr. Bo Le can only hold his whip and shout, "A fine horse is far away in the sky, looking out to Fusang, where can I find it?" Horse oh horse? Will it return?

Finally, I hope that the author of the article, Xun Ziju, after seeing this newspaper, will inform us of someone's communication address so that we can tell Mr. Bo Le, so that Bo Le can get the horse and the horse can meet Bo Le, wouldn't that be wonderful! (Address: Zhu Xinggong, No. 45, Renji Lane, Shanhai Pass Road, Shanghai)

The Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 30: Watching the Wailing Wild Geese, Guarding the Country with Buried Heads, Bullets Piercing Firmly, Blood Staining the Lonely City

Although he was silent, he also understood a great deal. It was as if someone was telling him in the dark that war was coming, that the foreshadowing of war was like this. From here, further imagining what the future of the war would be like was also conceivable. But as Ziqiang was in such a trance, he felt a gust of cool wind blowing past the corner of his mouth. This gust of wind served as a great warning to him. He followed up and remembered that he had just sworn an oath with the battalion commander to serve the country with utmost loyalty. Now, the blood from his mouth had not yet dried, and he was already thinking about how terrible the war was. For a soldier, fighting is his natural duty, so what is there to be afraid of? This is like a person who flies an airplane. Can you say that flying an airplane is scary? Thinking this, he puffed out his chest, cheered up, returned to his company headquarters, and continued his usual tasks. Nothing happened that night. The next day, after morning exercises and lectures, everyone seemed to be fine. At eleven o'clock, the brothers were in small groups, each holding a piece of corn bread made from mixed flour, squatting on the ground for lunch. At this moment, a buzzing sound occurred overhead. All the brothers had experienced war before. How could they not understand what this kind of sound meant? It was clear that the enemy's planes had arrived. Therefore, everyone was still listening with their ears pricked up while sending the corn bread in their hands to their mouths to hear the location of the sound. Fortunately, there were squad leaders supervising them, and when they saw this situation, they immediately shouted, "Eat, eat, what are you listening to? Listening is this situation, and not listening is this situation. After we are full, we still have to do our job." The officer said this, and the soldiers lowered their heads and ate. But at this moment, there was a earth-shaking sound, and a bomb landed and exploded. How would the villagers know how to avoid airplanes? Everyone started crying and shouting. (403)

Education News

Li Shizeng of the World Society Sends Off Eleven Young Children to Study Abroad: They Set Off Yesterday to the International School in Geneva

The World Society at 393 Fuxing Road, this city, held a farewell luncheon yesterday afternoon for thirteen Chinese teachers and students from World Schools going to Europe. Mr. Li Shizeng, a committee member, hosted the banquet.

This is likely the first time that Chinese children have been sent to study in Europe, starting with young students. A luncheon was held in the morning, and they boarded the ship at 6 PM in the afternoon to go abroad. Details are as follows:

Guests Present: The World Society held a luncheon yesterday afternoon to bid farewell to Chinese teachers and students from World Schools. In addition to the thirteen teachers and students, the attendees included invited guests and student parents. Among the Chinese and foreign guests present were Mona, a consultant to the National Economic Commission; Secretary Ma Su; Committee Member Zhang Jingjiang and his wife; Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Relief Committee; the wife of Ambassador to Japan Jiang Zuobin; Traditional Chinese Medicine practitioner Lu Zhong'an; and famous opera performers Cheng Yanqiu and Qi Yunqing, totaling over a hundred people.

Luncheon Details: The host and guests toasted each other at the banquet, creating a joyful atmosphere that lasted until after 1 PM. At the same time, a simple examination was held for the students, requiring each student to write their name and address at the Geneva school in Western languages, and to write a travel itinerary in Chinese. An oral exam was also conducted.

Names of Teachers and Students: The first and second group of students going to Geneva include teachers Mr. Pan, Mr. Xiang, Mr. Xie, and Mrs. Xie Hu, along with the following students: Lu Woruo (female, Hebei, 9 years old), Lu Furuo (female, Hebei, 10 years old), Hu Xiangxiong (male, Jiangsu, 10 years old), Xu Lianzi (female, Anhui, 10 years old), Zhang Naiqi (female, Zhejiang, 12 years old), Cheng Yongguang (male, Hebei, 10 years old), Jia Zhizhai (male, Hebei, 9 years old), Jiang Shuozhi (male, Hubei, 12 years old), Jiang Shuoping (male, Hubei, 11 years old), Qi Xiru (female, Hebei, 11 years old), and Qi Xiyao (female, Hebei, 9 years old), totaling eleven students.

Shipboard Curriculum: The course items designated to take place en route to Geneva are as follows (1) Chinese Language, (2) English, (3) Travel Knowledge, and (4) Journal.

Daily Schedule: 6:00 AM: Wake up, wash, take a walk, breakfast; 8:30 AM to 9:30 AM: English; 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM: Chinese Language; 12:00 PM: Lunch; 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM: Travel Knowledge; 6:00 PM: Dinner; 7:00 PM: Journal; 8:30 PM or 9:00 PM: Bedtime.

Report by Mr. Li: Mr. Li Shizeng, a committee member, gave a brief report at the farewell banquet, saying, "This report is titled 'A Report on World Schools...' What does this mean? It is a very simple overall report on the various organizations and issues of World Schools. A detailed explanation would not be possible given the limited space and time. However, saying only two things would be too incomplete. Therefore, I must use the style of 'concise and comprehensive.' Having defined this, I can briefly describe each section and item as follows:

World School: This school is located in Geneva, named École Internationale in French and International School in English. It has a history of many years, with dozens of teachers and hundreds of students of dozens of nationalities. The languages studied are English, French, and German. If the students are not nationals using these three languages, they will, of course, review and improve their native language. The purpose of this school is not only to have a global vision but also to be a factual product in an international environment. Switzerland is a key area in the international environment of Europe, and China is also a key area in the international environment. Although their natures are different, the need for several languages and global education has the same factual result. Therefore, China is a comrade country of the World School in Geneva, and there is a need to establish a World School in China or a Shanghai branch of the World School. This matter is being planned and prepared.

World Comrades: The World School Comrades Association is an organization formed by people who sympathize with the World School. There are World School American Comrades and World School Chinese Comrades... The school buildings of the World School were funded by the American Comrades Association. The Chinese Comrades Association was founded last year and does not yet have this strength, but it is working in this direction and will surely be impressive in the future. Its first task is to introduce six Chinese students to the school. This minimum goal has now been achieved and exceeded. This association will, of course, have parents, teachers, and students as current and future members. In a broad sense, teachers and students include not only faculty and staff but also all advocates and sponsors. There is a separate report and charter for the detailed organization of the association, so what is said here can only be extremely brief.

First Luncheon: The above is a brief description, and the content includes World School teachers, students, student parents, relatives, and guests. This association is very friendly, simple, and hastily organized. One or two parents (namely Mr. and Mrs. Zhang Jingjiang) wanted to have a gathering and farewell with the teachers who led the students to go abroad. At the same time, other parents and organizers also had the same idea, so they integrated it as a whole to avoid repetition. Directly and indirectly, many relatives and friends also joined, and there was no long-term and meticulous organization. The host and guests have reached a hundred people. Three teachers and ten students are the main guests, and others are the hosts. There are also a few guests who happened to be there or were only invited by the host to accompany them. This luncheon seems to be held every time students go abroad in the future. This is not only the first luncheon but also the first chapter in the history of Chinese students at World Schools.

Teachers and Students Going to Europe: The first and second groups of Chinese teachers and students at World Schools are listed together because it is difficult to distinguish the first and second times. This is the first official organization. Although there were fewer people in the unofficial one, there was one last year. There was only one teacher and one student. The difference between formal and informal is a long story. In the past, the government did not allow children to go abroad except for those traveling with their parents. Starting this time, it has been officially permitted. Therefore, this is not only the first time that students from World Schools have officially gone abroad but also the first time that Chinese students have officially gone abroad, at least since the Republic of China. There are four teachers leading the students to go abroad:

Mr. Xiang teaches Chinese language and Sinology

Mr. Lian teaches temporary education

Mr. Pan represents the parents

Mr. Xie Hu teaches Chinese language and Sinology

Mr. Kang went abroad last year, and Mr. Pan, Mr. Xiang, and Mr. Xie are going abroad this time.

Director Pan of the Municipal Education Bureau Talks about Children's Tuberculosis: 16 Million People in Our Country Suffer from Tuberculosis: Most Contracted During Childhood: Handle Injections, Examinations, and Recuperation, etc., Separately

Mr. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, spoke on the left about the past examinations and future relief of the many elementary school students in this city suffering from lung disease:

Attention to Health Education

Since its establishment, this city has attached great importance to children's health education. Since Mr. Gongzhan took office as the Director of the Education Bureau in the autumn of the year before last, he has made health education the central business of various education programs and has received the full cooperation of the Health Bureau. Therefore, the advancement of health education is fast.

Tuberculosis Examination

This spring, with the assistance of Dr. Gao Xianglang of the Chinese Red Cross Society, we began to handle tuberculosis examinations for elementary school students to prevent and treat tuberculosis. Hundreds of millions of people die from tuberculosis every year. According to accurate statistics, the world's tuberculosis death rate is 100,000 people as a unit. New Zealand's death rate is 51 people, Egypt's 72 people, the United States' 79 people, Germany's 89 people, the United Kingdom's 103 people, Spain's 136 people, Italy's 188 people, Japan's 186 people, and our country's death rate has reached 307 people. In total, 16 million people in our country suffer from this disease. On average, one in every 25 people suffers from this disease, and 80% of this disease is contracted during childhood.

Cooperation Between Home and School

Children do not realize that they have this disease at first and play as usual. If it is found at this time and treated early, they can be completely cured. Therefore, the Health Bureau and this bureau have specially requested pediatricians to first hold free tuberculosis injections and examinations at the Municipal Xicheng and Bide Elementary Schools. This injection is simpler than vaccination and has minimal reactions. There is no pain during the test. In advance, this bureau instructed the school to notify the family members and explain the reasons in detail. A parents' meeting was also held, and Dr. Gao gave a lecture to proceed.

Many Patients

Among the students examined, Xicheng had 397 people and Bide had 820 people. Xicheng had 262 people with positive reactions, and Bide had 542 people. The percentage of people suspected of infection accounted for 66%. However, the 66% of children with positive reactions may not all have tuberculosis, or may only be slightly infected and not yet sick. Therefore, the second step is to perform a detailed lung examination.

Treatment Methods

A lung examination with X-rays is available, but the price is quite expensive. The Red Cross only charges a material fee of three yuan. To serve the country, the treatment methods are based on the individual's condition and the current situation, and are handled in three different ways: (1) For the mildest cases, normal schooling will continue, but parents are requested to provide special nutrition and care, and to take cod liver oil for a long time (currently redesigned by Section Chief Wu Liguo of the Health Bureau to avoid the fishy taste). (2) For slightly ill individuals, reduce class and work hours, rest for two hours each in the morning, or study in the morning and rest in the afternoon, and add tonics. (3) For more serious cases, immediately seek medical treatment. Fortunately, very few cases are found to be severe after examination.

Continuation of Testing

It has recently been rumored that many students at Xicheng and Bide schools suffer from tuberculosis, and it is planned not to send children to school. In fact, this is not the case. If students from other schools are examined, there will also be similar alarming news. This is not only a problem for one school or one country; the whole world is suffering from the harm of tubercle bacilli. Next semester, this bureau and others will continue to invite Dr. Gao Jinglang and others to continue to carry out injections and tests for students from other schools.

Improvement of Treatment

In the future, regarding the relief of students with pulmonary tuberculosis and weak students, within the scope of economic possibilities, we should try to provide treatment in many ways, such as establishing a children's sanatorium in the municipal hospital, implementing sun lamp irradiation, sunbathing, open-air schools, and school meals in schools. This summer vacation, this bureau and others plan to jointly open summer nutrition classes in Gaoqiao, Wusong and other places with the Health Bureau, which is also for this reason. Since the government is working hard in the front, we deeply hope that the people will work hard in the rear. It is fortunate for the nation and fortunate for the country.

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau instructed 73 private schools, including the YMCA Middle School, stating: "In the case of the previous application by the school to allocate the 1934 educational subsidy from the Public Works Bureau of the First Special District, this bureau has sent personnel to investigate, carefully reviewed, and forwarded it to the Public Works Bureau for verification. The Ministry of Education Approves the Shanghai Middle School Progress Outline The Education Bureau Will Immediately Announce Its Implementation

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, in order to promote the balanced development of various subjects in various middle schools, has compiled a plan outline for the teaching progress of various subjects in middle schools. The outline has been approved by the Ministry of Education and will be announced for implementation. The outline is extracted as follows:

(1) Principles: The detailed teaching items for each subject are compiled based on the principle of complying with the curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry, but with reference to the local environment and teaching principles, modifications can be made. (2) Classification of Teaching Progress Tables (hereinafter referred to as this table): The following types are divided: high school includes eight subjects: Chinese, Mathematics, Physics, Chemistry, Biology, History, Geography, and Foreign Languages; junior high school includes nine subjects: Chinese, Mathematics, Botany, Zoology, Physics, Chemistry, History, Geography, and Foreign Languages. Civics will be compiled after the standards are set by the Ministry. A teaching progress record book will be compiled separately for each subject for teachers in each school to fill in during implementation. (3) Quantity: The quantity of each subject should be in accordance with Article 9 of the Middle School Regulations promulgated by the Ministry, which stipulates the academic year, semester vacation, and the academic qualifications stipulated in this city. After deducting commemorative days, holidays, Sundays, review experiments, and examination time, the actual number of teaching days per semester is approximately 108 days, which is 18 weeks. This table is based on this number of weeks. (4) Quality: The quality of each subject must focus on the leadership of thought and the training of personality. For subjects such as Chinese, History, Geography, and Foreign Languages, special attention must be paid to the cultivation of national spirit and the understanding of national conditions. For subjects such as Mathematics, Physics, Chemistry, and Biology, the focus is on recognizing life interests, and emphasizing the training of skills in thinking, observation, and utilization of nature. (5) Form: Each progress table and progress record book is prefaced with a detailed explanation of the progress table. Each type is divided into weeks, and each week is divided into four items: teaching hours, outline, detailed items, and remarks. Each type of progress record book is divided into months, and each semester is divided into books, with each book divided into three items: teaching outline, teaching material summary, and remarks. (6) Reference: The compilation committee of each group should prepare the following reference books: 1. Curriculum standards promulgated by the Ministry; 2. Academic qualifications in this city; 3. Teaching progress tables for the subject in other provinces and cities; 4. Textbooks for the subject approved by the Ministry; 5. Progress tables for the subject in famous schools; 6. Other important reference books on the subject. Items 1 to 5 above will be collected and distributed to each group committee by this bureau. Item 6 will be collected by the members of each group themselves. (7) Steps: This bureau will hire experts in each subject as compilation committee members to hold a full compilation committee meeting to discuss and jointly compile standards. Then, the chairmen of each subject will hold a group compilation committee meeting to study the detailed items of each subject and begin compilation. After the compilation is completed, it will be sent to this bureau for review and opinions will be sought from experts. After the review is completed, a full compilation committee meeting will be held to report the review opinions and return them to the compilation committee members of each group for revision. After the revision, it will be sent to this bureau for printing. (8) Deadline: From May 11th to September , a total of fifteen weeks, with eight weeks for compilation, one week for review, one week for revision, and four weeks for printing. (9) Implementation: After printing is completed, this bureau will announce and implement it. Starting from the first semester of the 23rd year, all public and private middle schools in this city must teach according to the progress table, and teachers in each school must fill in the record book on time to match the progress. At the end of each month, each school will compile the teaching progress record books for each subject and submit them to this bureau for review. They will be returned to each school at the end of the semester. The test questions for examinations and joint examinations will be based on the progress table.

Sports Meeting Methods 1. Track and field events will be held once a year in mid-May, and the location will be permanently in the provincial capital. 2. Each school may enter up to two people in each event, and each person may enter up to two events. They are divided into high school and junior high school, and each department is not divided into groups. 3. Equipment performances and track and field events will be held at the same time, and five types will be determined: horizontal bars, parallel bars, wooden horses, vaulting boxes, and hanging rings. The sports funding for secondary schools should be implemented in accordance with the National Sports Implementation Plan and determine the method of spending. (Resolution) Based on the National Sports Implementation Plan, regarding funding, each school should allocate a portion of the school's regular expenses for the implementation of the sports curriculum, except for staff salaries and sports construction. As for student sports fees (except for normal schools and rural normal schools), they should be used exclusively for the needs of sports equipment inside and outside the classroom. The department will issue an order to each school to implement it from the 23rd year. 7. How should the leave of absence for girls' sports class examples (referring to the period of menstruation for women) be implemented? (Resolution) Pass the method (Method) 1. Women must take leave during menstruation. Teachers must never force students during menstruation to participate in sports except for gentle exercises such as performing soft exercises and morning exercises. 2. Morning exercises must continue without interruption. 3. Example students must still attend classes at the same time as other students. However, within the possible range, teachers will designate appropriate activities, such as billiards, table golf, and nine-pin bowling. 4. The number of days of leave is limited to three days each time. Those who take more than three days must obtain special permission from the physical education teacher. 11. Can Tai Chi exercises be included in the game gymnastics program to promote implementation? (Resolution) Each school can adopt it freely. 12. Each school should hire more full-time physical education teachers and reduce the number of teaching hours for each teacher in order to improve teaching effectiveness. (Resolution) It is recommended that the Education Department handle it as appropriate.

Guessing the Wimbledon Champion There Is Actually a Gambling Company Strange Events in British Tennis Abound Pan Lai pays one to three, Crawford pays one to four

(London Correspondence) This year's Wimbledon Tennis Championships will begin on June 25th. Strangely enough, a company has been established to gamble on this year's wins and losses, with the focus on guessing who will be the men's singles champion this year. This is the first time in the history of the Wimbledon Championships. The company has printed a list of players in alphabetical order and attached the number of payouts after guessing correctly. The numbers are as follows:

Pan Lai pays one to three, Crawford pays one to four

Austin pays one to four, Hills pays one to eight

Ailvsen pays one to eight, A Borogella pays twenty

Stokesfen pays one to twenty, McGrath pays one to twenty-five

The largest payout is one to two hundred, such as Silly, Mitsugi, Dorgate, Dinkin, Sharp, Orlev, and other unpopular players. The company's conditions are as follows: regardless of whether the player participates, the bet will not be refunded. For those who reach the quarter-finals, half of the payout will be paid. Wimbledon gambling has never been so prevalent. This gambling company is afraid of losing money. No one dares to try to pay one to five, let alone risk paying one to two hundred.

Newspapers are betting on Pan Lai to win, but according to the opinions of some experts, it belongs to Crawford. I would rather get one to four than Pan Lai's one to three.

Borogella's one to twenty is the most ridiculous, because Bao has already decided not to participate in the singles competition. McGrath's one to twenty-five is the most promising dark horse.

All of Shanghai Open Handball Singles Zhu Kuan Wins the Championship The Doubles Championship Was Also Won by Zhu Kuan and Hong Yukui A Glorious Page in the History of Chinese Sports

The first All Shanghai Open Singles and Doubles Handball Championships initiated by the YMCA attracted many Western athletes. Among the Chinese who joined, the singles included Xia Zeren, Sun Daosheng (third place in this competition), and Zhu Kuan. The doubles only included Zhu Kuan and Hong Yukui. In addition to Zhu and Hong winning the doubles championship a few days ago, Mr. Zhu won the All Shanghai Singles Championship yesterday after two fierce battles with a score of 21 to 19 and 22 to 20, which is truly a glorious page in the history of Chinese sports. The intensity of the battle at that time was unprecedented. The details are described below.

Winners of the open handball, from right to left: Hong Yukui, Zhu Kuan (doubles champion and Zhu is the singles champion), Sun Daosheng (third in singles), Qian Yiqin (coach) (photographed by Qichang)

Mr. Zhu won the first serve, but was immediately taken away by Chaka. Both sides strictly defended and attacked. After more than ten minutes, they only scored eight points each. Suddenly, Mr. Cha's spirits were lifted, and he scored many points in a row, creating an advantage of 18 to 12. At this time, Mr. Zhu was unwilling to show weakness and counterattacked vigorously, chasing to 20, and was regained by Mr. Cai for one point. However, Mr. Zhu saw the opportunity and immediately regained it, winning the last point with an unexpected victory, becoming 21 to 19, and winning the first game.

Mr. Cai served first. After fifteen rounds, both sides only scored three points each. Then, Mr. Zhu's kills were fierce, taking a lead of 10 to 6. Although Mr. Cai followed closely behind, he also scored several points, but he could not surpass Mr. Zhu. The recent score was 12 to 11, still led by Mr. Zhu. Then, both sides fought more and more fiercely. Mr. Cai once tied the score at 15, but Mr. Zhu gained four points, creating an advantage of 19 to 15. But soon

Mr. Cai tried his best to fight hard and chased to 18 points. At this time, both sides were exhausted. Mr. Zhu regained one point, becoming 20 to 18. However, Mr. Cai took the opportunity to regain two points, becoming a tie of 20 each. Fortunately, Mr. Zhu was quick-witted and scored two points, winning the final victory, and winning the singles championship in this competition.

On the whole, Mr. Zhu's ball skills are actually better than Mr. Cai's. However, Mr. Cai made many saves yesterday, and his left hand has made rapid progress after a week of practice. He is physically strong, but his wisdom is far inferior to Mr. Zhu's. Currently, the market value of the new scale is about 2.67 yuan, and new goods are still expected to fall. Yesterday at the foreign tea market in this port, interest in Zhenmei green tea from Tunxi, Sui'an, Wenzhou, and other regions, handled by Yingzhuang Jinlong, Yihe Xiehe, Tianxiang Huacha, and Tianyu firms, was keen. Suzhou and Zhejiang Silkworm Cocoons Are Scarce

The Pingyao cocoon market is gradually closing. New cocoons have been on the market in the Pingyao area of Yuyao for over ten days. Cocoon merchants are offering low prices, with the highest price for improved varieties being only twenty yuan, and the lowest price for native varieties being fourteen yuan and fifty cents. Farmers are all selling at a loss. The amount of goods arriving on the market is decreasing, and cocoon merchants are gradually closing their scales.

The best improved variety of cocoons is from Lin'an. The model sericulture area of Lin'an has had a bountiful harvest of improved silkworm breeds. The quality of the cocoons is also better, while native varieties are slightly inferior. Cocoon merchants have been weighing and purchasing cocoons for over ten days, and the amount of goods arriving on the market is still high. The price of improved varieties is thirty yuan, while native varieties are seventeen or eighteen yuan, causing farmers to suffer losses.

Most silkworm farmers in Liyang are losing money. Farmers in the four rural areas of Liyang raised a good number of silkworms this year, but there was a shortage of leaves, and leaf prices were not stable, resulting in high costs. Cocoon merchants are weighing and purchasing cocoons according to the prices agreed upon by the industry association, with improved varieties selling for fifteen to thirty yuan per sima catty and native varieties selling for fourteen to eighteen yuan. As a result, most silkworm farmers are losing money. The opening price for new cocoons in Haimen is not high. Cocoon merchants in the various sandbar areas of Haimen have been opening their scales for three or four days. The weather this year has been unfavorable, and farmers have suffered significant losses of native silkworms. The production of improved cocoons is still abundant, but cocoon prices are not high, with improved varieties selling for twenty to twenty-five yuan and native varieties selling for fourteen to eighteen yuan. Silkworm farmers are selling with reluctance.

Zhejiang Spring Cocoon Production Volume. This year, Zhejiang province distributed 600,000 sheets of improved breeds in each sericulture area. Each sheet of silkworms produced a maximum of 50 catties of cocoons, and a minimum of 20 catties. Overall there were 18,000,000 dan of fresh cocoons produced for a very plentiful harvest. The cocoons are also said to be high quality.

Overseas silk sales are becoming increasingly sluggish. Due to slow sales of silk fabrics, overseas silk weaving factories are trying to reduce production, and raw silk mills are becoming less active. Japanese silk is still being sold aggressively, and silk prices in New York and Lyon have fallen to their lowest levels. There is no news about Chinese silk. European and American firms in Shanghai are considering lowering prices and stockpiling goods, making it difficult for Chinese merchants to sell at a loss. The market atmosphere is increasingly sluggish, with no transactions reported.

Free Talk

On Human Nature

— Fei Xin

There is a riddle in mythology about a person who has four feet in the morning, two feet at noon, and three feet in the evening.

A child crawling on the ground and an old man using a cane are not much different. Pure, innocent. If we say that human nature is not empty, and that there are two natures, divine and human, then divinity can be said to be most pronounced in these two periods. The god-like form and the transcendent, primitive soul.

Children of all races, black and yellow, are indistinguishable when they are together, because their blood is all crimson red. Old people of all races, black and yellow, are also indistinguishable when they are together, because their hair is all white. Only in the middle of life are there differences in nation and race; there are politics and diplomatic games. And their blood is green or black.

Confucius's three cautions—against lust, against strife, and against greed—can be said to understand human nature. They refer to these busy people. They also implicitly agree with the Buddhist cautions against delusion, hatred, and greed, although the latter are broader. The vague teachings of philosophers seem no more foolish than those of clever people, but rather a little cleverer, so they say such things. Those with four feet and those with three feet are not included. Only in the age of two feet, after satisfying food and lust, is it most frightening.

If divinity is submerged and the soul is destroyed, then what remains is the purely materialistic middle-aged person, who is most pitiful. At this time, like a drowning person, one frantically tries to grasp something, seeking to survive in the crowd or to transcend the crowd, forcefully clinging to everything. There is often a hidden terror, thinking, "Once I die, will there be nothing left?" Thus, one strives to cling, allowing human nature to develop to the extreme, belonging to nothing, and creating all kinds of sins.

And time is mercilessly passing, unknowingly deteriorating with fortune. If one slightly reflects, one realizes that all that is clung to is illusory, truly "everything is empty." Recalling one's life, regret arises everywhere, still frantic. If divinity is restored at this time, and one is subjected to invisible whipping, then it can be said to be human hell!

Those who understand the morning and evening of life, if they slightly examine themselves, will slightly change their actions! The world will also undergo some changes.

Another Proposal丨Regarding the Reprinting of Ancient Books丨

— Xu Maoyong

Having read Mr. Yuan's "Proposal to Those Reprinting Ancient Books" in the "Literature" "Special Issue on Chinese Literature Research," I would like to share some ideas that I have long held in my heart.

My opinion is this: For ancient books that have lasting value and are needed by most people, such as the "Twenty-Four Histories," they should be reprinted with inferior paper and smaller fonts, so that they can be sold at the lowest possible price and widely circulated.

Book scholars or collectors with money probably would not understand the benefits of the above-mentioned method of printing ancient books, but most readers will surely understand. For example, an ordinary stone-printed copy of "Water Margin" costs at least one yuan, but there is a kind of inferior copy on the market that only costs two or three jiao. Why is it so cheap? Naturally, it is because the paper is inferior, the printing is poor, and, because it is a reprint of an ancient book, manuscript fees and royalties are also saved, so the cost is indeed low. Perhaps there are other reasons that make the cost even lower than the above, but these are unknown to an outsider like myself who is not in the publishing industry.

Because it is cheap, many people buy it. Whether in the city or in the countryside, these kinds of books are extremely popular. On the bookshelves of college students who do not like to buy books, next to the dressing tables of modern young ladies who do not know what books are, and together with textbooks, one can often find several kinds of inferior copies of "Wenxin Diaolong," "Su Huang's Letters," "Shishuo Xinyu," and "Peony Pavilion." Because they are merely decorations, these kinds of books are also bound in Western style, making them look good. As for the counters of small shop clerks and the pillows of rural teachers, these kinds of "Seven Heroes and Five Gallants," "Dream of the Red Chamber," and "Anthology of Ancient Prose" have almost completely replaced the previous stone-printed copies, because these kinds are letterpress printed and have modern punctuation marks, making them look much more refreshing than the stone-printed copies, and the price is cheaper than the stone-printed copies.

These kinds of printed books are worthy of promotion; only they can circulate widely and become popular among readers. However, unfortunately, the publishing houses that are currently printing these kinds of books are only reprinting ordinary novels and notes, which can only be used by general low-level readers for entertainment. Large-scale, valuable books are not being printed. Therefore, this matter cannot yet be said to have made any good contributions to the cultural world, and because it always caters to low-level tastes and publishes boring novels, it will instead poison the majority of readers.

Therefore, I have a proposal for these publishing houses: use the same method to systematically and planfully reprint large-scale, valuable ancient masterpieces. In my opinion, if the "Twenty-Four Histories" were also reprinted in this way, then readers could buy them for only a few dollars, and as a result, many people would definitely buy them, and the reprinting houses could still make money. If they could do this, then their contribution to the cultural world would be far greater than that of other houses that are photolithographically printing "Rare Books from the Siku Quanshu" and finely printing "Sibu Beiyao." Even the "Basic Collection of National Studies" that Mr. Yuan praised is still printed too well and sold too expensively for most readers.

Of course, errors are inevitable in this kind of edition, because the manufacturing is close to being crude. But for the average reader, encountering a few errors is really not a big deal. There are many books that, rather than not being able to read at all, it is better to read with errors. Reading will always be more beneficial than not reading. Moreover, are there not also many errors in those books that are photolithographically printed in Song Dynasty fonts?

Visiting Sai Jinhua

— Zijin

On a rare, drizzly afternoon in Beijing, five of us, newcomers from the South, were guided by Mr. He, a long-time resident of the ancient capital, to visit Tianqiao, Beijing's entertainment district for the poor.

We spent a few copper coins to listen to the raspy-voiced girls sing drum lyrics, watched boxing matches and medicine peddlers, monkey shows, and the strange things at various stalls. As we walked to the entrance of a narrow, dirty alley, Mr. He pointed and said, "Sai Jinhua lives in there." His casual remark aroused our curiosity. We pleaded, "Take us to see her!"

We walked into this narrow alley lined with low houses and stood outside a pair of dilapidated gates. We saw a paper strip pasted on the gate with the four large characters "Jiangxi Wei Residence." We knocked on the door, and a woman in her fifties came out to open it. She seemed to know Mr. He, and without asking, she let us in. After passing through a narrow, cluttered courtyard, Sai Jinhua's bedroom was on the left. We walked into that dark, small room full of broken objects. The room really couldn't hold all six of us, so those who came later had to stand by the threshold.

The arrival of this group of strangers clearly disturbed everyone in the room. As soon as we entered, a man in his forties walked out from the inner room, followed by a woman dressed in simple black clothing. According to Mr. He's introduction, she was Sai Jinhua. She greeted Mr. He peacefully. After clarifying our intentions, she immediately said, "My place is very simple, please don't laugh! Please sit, please sit!"

Everything in the room, all the furnishings, seemed to be symbols of Sai Jinhua's difficult, miserable, and melancholic life in her later years.

This beauty from Suzhou, whose enchanting name once stirred up a sensation, captivated countless men of letters, refined scholars, heroes, and magnates, and who "once sat with the British Emperor for a photograph, a remarkable event in contemporary opinion," was now only wearing a tattered black cotton-padded jacket and pants, with yellowish cotton peeking out from the holes. The glory and wealth of her past seemed to have completely escaped from her, leaving her with only poverty, disease, and suffering.

"How old are you this year, madam?" Mr. O asked.

"Just sixty years old. I'm old, useless, often sick, and very poor!"

Her plaintive answer couldn't help but surprise us. In her fair skin, lively demeanor, and clear voice, we could only see a middle-aged woman of about forty at most. She didn't look old or frail at all. No matter what, we couldn't believe she was already an old woman of sixty. However, her face was palely pitiable. This was probably because, as she said, poverty led to malnutrition, and sickness often accompanied her.

"How do you make a living now?" Mr. B asked sympathetically.

"I'm completely destitute. I don't know about tomorrow. For the past year or two, I've been relying on my mother's remaining clothes and jewelry to exchange for money. I really don't know how I'll live after that..." Her eyes, which were once captivating in her youth, were now filled with tears.

"What are your plans for the future?" Mr. B asked with sympathy.

"I have no way at all. What plans can a sixty-year-old woman have?... But I want to go back to the South. I still have my sister-in-law, nephews, and nieces in Suzhou. I want to go back and see them. Jiangnan must be full of birdsong and flowers now, right? Some gentlemen from the South, tell me about the scenery of Jiangnan!"

"..."

"I have a wish now: I want to return to Jiangnan and find a piece of land in Hangzhou for a burial plot. As the saying goes, 'Live in Suzhou, die in Hangzhou.' I only have this little wish now. But this is obviously just a dream..." she said with unspeakable sadness.

"That's easy to do!" Ms. A consoled her.

"..."

"I also want to become a vegetarian and practice religion," she said, as if calming down.

"..."

"Madam, please serve tea to the guests," the woman in her fifties who led us in brought in tea and snacks. Sai Jinhua glanced at her, turned her head, and told us, "This is a loyal servant! She has served me since I was young, all the way until now. I don't have the money to hire her now, but she is willing to suffer with me!"

The eyes of all six of us turned to this maidservant. She had a face of loyalty, endurance, courage, and a strong body.

We had tea, took a photo of Sai Jinhua, and then said goodbye.

As we walked out of the gate, everyone recited the same two lines of poetry:

"Desolate and deserted before the gate, few carriages and horses come; in old age, she married a merchant!"

(May 12, 1934)

Frog Song

— Wang Yixin

The song of the frogs is like a downpour

Sprinkling on the lonely fields;

A sense of nervous energy

Painted on this quiet village night.

××××

It follows you, right and left,

Like stars filling the sky;

A bustling night music

Plays out the daytime tension of farm work.

Spring by the Side of Solitary Beauty Peak

— Yingbing

The sun is shining and people are already feeling a little hot, and the wind doesn't blow as coldly as before. This is spring!

The spring in Jiangnan is considered to be very enviable weather, but the spring in the South is even better, especially making me constantly think of the spring by the side of Solitary Beauty Peak.

"Guilin's scenery is the best in the world," this is a sentence everyone knows. In fact, when it comes to our Guangxi, there are mountains and water everywhere, with very beautiful natural scenery.

As soon as you enter Guangxi's gate—Wuzhou, whether you go to Liuzhou by the Liu River or to Guilin by the Fu River, you will see "mountains and water" along the way. The water seems to flow in the gaps between the mountains, and the mountains are continuous and stretch out: there are dense forests on the mountains, villages at the foot of the mountains, vegetable plots by the river, and willow trees... There are fishing boats by the river. When spring arrives, everything you see is a refreshing scene. The boat travels between the mountains, and you often encounter the feeling of "having exhausted the mountains and rivers and suspecting there is no road," but when you turn a corner, it suddenly becomes clear.

If you arrive in Guilin, the scenery is certainly quite beautiful, worthy of others' praise, among which the most outstanding is Solitary Beauty Peak.

Solitary Beauty Peak is in the center of the city, behind the Jingjiang Prince's Mansion of the Ming Dynasty. Now a Sun Yat-sen Memorial Pagoda has been built next to Solitary Beauty Peak, surrounding Solitary Beauty Peak to form a Sun Yat-sen Park. Solitary Beauty Peak is as straight as a pen, large at the bottom and small at the top, and even smaller at the top point. There are several small temples, which look like a pen tip from a distance. It is not high, with 365 steps. There is a pond at the foot of the peak—Crescent Moon Pond. In spring, the water rises, and you can go boating inside. There is a pavilion in the pond, connected to the two banks by a winding bridge.

In the past, we studied at the school next to Solitary Beauty Peak, and Sun Yat-sen Park was our campus. In spring, there are especially many tourists, and the scenery is especially beautiful. The flowers and grass seem to be taller for the happy tourists. Ping, Hua, and Fen and I have all been happy tourists in the happy spring. What about now? Ping, Hua, and Fen, I haven't known their news for a long time.

Beautiful spring by the side of Solitary Beauty Peak, I think you will not lose color without us. Now spring has come again, and some spring feelings and spring meanings cannot help but make me think of the precious time of the past spring by the side of Solitary Beauty Peak.

Ninety-Ninth

Fire Disaster (4)

— Fei'er

I then received many old friends. They all seemed a little older, and everyone had lost that old lively and cheerful color, as if they had gone through a disaster, and everyone had changed into another person. It was the same with my old classmate Zhang Wentian—the boss of Fuhe Company—who used to be a lively child. Ten years ago, we had ridden bicycles and raced on forest paths, and we had also rowed Malay boats and raced in tidal rivers. Now he was much more mature, showing that he was an adult carrying a heavy burden, and his face was even that of a merchant planning and strategizing.

He invited me to a banquet held at their store at 10:30 in the evening, organized by a group of young people to welcome me.

At dinner time, I talked with my uncle about the recent situation of relatives, the situation in Tangshan, and some news from Southeast Asia. I drank a little wine with the old man, and then walked out of here and ran to Fuhe Company in the third room on the left. I heard that my uncle's affairs had not been completed, and it was not convenient for me to bother him. Moreover, it was more free to talk there, and the actions could be more unrestrained.

The scene in Fuhe Company's store was almost as lonely, but the goods were piled up even more than in my relative's store. Because it was night, the dim light reflected on the cold glass showcases, and the scene felt even more desolate. When Mr. Zhang saw me coming, he greeted me enthusiastically and invited me to drink a cup or two of Chaozhou "Kung Fu Tea." Although I don't drink much tea now, I had tasted the taste and poetry of this antique tea ten years ago. Now, drinking this very strong tea, although a bit bitter, the enthusiasm of old friends is sweet, so I had to drink some.

Because it was early, he accompanied me to stroll through the several streets in this small village market. Although there were scattered shops and houses on these streets, they could not block the coconut groves and betel nut trees that were exposed on both sides of the road. In the quieter streets, "Atap Houses" still vaguely flashed, and the original flavor of this village was well preserved. In the past, we often spent good evenings here, when the sun went down and the evening coolness arrived. I had been thinking that I probably would not be able to appreciate this beautiful scenery again, but who knew that I would taste this meaning again now?
